  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9779998216395147828">Finnikin of the Rock and his guardian, Sir Topher, have not been home to their beloved Lumatere for ten years. Not since the dark days when the royal family was murdered and the kingdom put under a terrible curse. But then Finnikin is summoned to meet Evanjalin, a young woman with an incredible claim: the heir to the throne of Lumatere, Prince Balthazar, is alive.<br/><br/>Evanjalin</span>
  <span id="freeText9779998216395147828" style="display:none">Finnikin of the Rock and his guardian, Sir Topher, have not been home to their beloved Lumatere for ten years. Not since the dark days when the royal family was murdered and the kingdom put under a terrible curse. But then Finnikin is summoned to meet Evanjalin, a young woman with an incredible claim: the heir to the throne of Lumatere, Prince Balthazar, is alive.<br /><br />Evanjalin is determined to return home and she is the only one who can lead them to the heir. As they journey together, Finnikin is affected by her arrogance . . . and her hope. He begins to believe he will see his childhood friend, Prince Balthazar, again. And that their cursed people will be able to enter Lumatere and be reunited with those trapped inside. He even believes he will find his imprisoned father.<br /><br />But Evanjalin is not what she seems. And the truth will test not only Finnikin's faith in her . . . but in himself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9779998216395147828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<a href="/questions/318893-does-this-book-contain-swearing-and-or">Does this book contain swearing and/or sexual content? Because if it doesn&#39;t, it sounds like my kind of book; and I&#39;m really hoping it is!!!</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_318893'><a id="like_count_community_question_318893" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/318893?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">5 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F4932435-finnikin-of-the-rock">like</a></span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/39137180-maris-bave"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1421623099i/39137180._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/39137180-maris-bave">Maris Bave</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Only a little swearing, but there is some very odd sexual content. At times the author seems very shy of anything sexual, like an extremely awkward co<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Only a little swearing, but there is some very odd sexual content. At times the author seems very shy of anything sexual, like an extremely awkward conversation between a girl and some men about her period. There is an attempted rape, but I believe the other answer that says "it is not graphic" is very true. At other times, talking of sexual abuse seems to be normal and the characters are unabashed about it. It's a little weird, but to answer your original question, there is both swearing and sexual content although not graphic and the swearing is rare and much lighter than other books. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's marketed as YA but is almost as mature as Game of Thrones. I'd say 14+. It's got quite a bit of violence, mention of rape, and later books in the<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's marketed as YA but is almost as mature as Game of Thrones. I'd say 14+. It's got quite a bit of violence, mention of rape, and later books in the series have non-explicit sex scenes.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_356471272" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/356471272" />
    <a title="Nataliya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya"><img alt="Nataliya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605995014p2/3672777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/356471272?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nataliya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nataliya" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya">Nataliya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780763651756" href="/book/show/7958284-finnikin-of-the-rock">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Nataliya by: </span>
      Many, many, oh so many overwhelmingly positive GR reviews
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer356471272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6389399312093673524">Dear <i>Finnikin of the Rock</i>, what happened? You and I were supposed to be enjoying the beginning of a beautiful friendship, walking into the sunset together.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380382072i/739587._SX540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Alas, no walking into the sunset was meant for us.</b> Instead, our date ended with me awkwardly fumbling for keys and muttering, <i>"Well, I'll call you sometime, I guess"</i>, knowing very well that you also acutely felt the absence of that proverbial chemistry, that necessary spark, and that none of us would be reaching for the phone any time soon. <br/><br/>De</span>
  <span id="freeText6389399312093673524" style="display:none">Dear <i>Finnikin of the Rock</i>, what happened? You and I were supposed to be enjoying the beginning of a beautiful friendship, walking into the sunset together.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380382072i/739587._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Alas, no walking into the sunset was meant for us.</b> Instead, our date ended with me awkwardly fumbling for keys and muttering, <i>"Well, I'll call you sometime, I guess"</i>, knowing very well that you also acutely felt the absence of that proverbial chemistry, that necessary spark, and that none of us would be reaching for the phone any time soon. <br><br>Dear <i>Finnikin of the Rock</i>, you *do* understand why I thought it was going to work out, right? You seemed to have the whole package, after all. <br><br>(1) <b>A medieval-ish fantasy setting</b> with strong emphasis on the modern-day values of tolerance and political correctness (judge me all you want, but I believe in getting rid of any 'authenticity' when it comes to misogyny and other forms of intolerance in my pleasure reads). <br>(2) <b>A strong-willed female protagonist</b> who is NEVER in any need of rescuing. <br>(3) <b>Melina Marchetta's prose</b> which I have praised before on several occasions. <br><br><b>
  <i>What's not to like, right? Right?? Right???</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380382072i/739588._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But just like in the aforementioned "Friends" episode, <b>the delicious-seeming ingredients just did not produce a mind-blowing final product</b> - to my utmost disappointment and sadness. Sadness, you hear that? Because I *wanted* it to work out between me and this book! <i>(I mean, Catie liked it, and she's my go-to person for good books - so what's *wrong* with me???)</i><br><br>I think my first stumbling point was <b>the puzzling childishness of this story</b> - including the 'epic' bits and all the 'dangers' the characters faced. <b>Never ever, not even for a moment, was there any sense of danger to our characters.</b> Never ever was there a feeling that they are about to embark on a journey that could be painful and lead to losses. No, nothing like that - even if we are faced with prison mines, a battlefield, a refugee camp plagued by deathly illness. No, everything was presented in a bright and happy light simply as another adventure at the end of which Finnikin and friends would - of course! - come out victorious, with no lasting consequences, physically and mentally, with Finnikin perpetually acting like a lovable brat and inevitably earning some appreciation from one or more father figures. Yeah.<br><br>My second stumbling block was the characterization of Evanjalin. <b>I think there is a difference between a strong female character who is able to be a tough leader - and a bratty liar who is worshiped, for no apparent reason, by everyone she comes in contact with.</b> So many things would have been much easier (and much less frustrating) had Evanjalin at any time decided to just talk to her companions instead of manipulating them into doing what works for her.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380382072i/739589._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And what does everyone do after learning about the aforementioned manipulation and lies? If you guessed that they treat her like gold, you're right. Because clearly she knows what's better for everyone, and is qualified to make choices for others.<br><br>Thirdly, a question - <b>how exactly does the nation of slightly over 6000 people develop several ethnic subgroups that are very distinct and apparently almost never intermix, all while living in close proximity?</b> In a nation where it appears everyone knows each other and each other's business - and yet they manage to not intermix and lose their very distinct physical characteristics? It just does not appear possible, and felt quite grating throughout the story.<br><br><b>Fourthly, so many storylines and ideas seemed to be introduced just to be dismissed a few pages later.</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<i>Froi attempting to rape Evanjalin?</i> That could have been a source of quite a bit of a story development - but no, it's kinda there and then shrugged off. <i>Evanjalin and the priest-king getting sick with the fever?</i> Nevermind, all is behind-the-scenes fine without anything ever coming out of it. <i>Being attacked by a seemingly brutal tribe?</i> Nevermind, we'll tell them a story and they will instantly become our BFFs! <i>An upset man whose beloved has a child with another man?</i> Nevermind, it's all connected to the spirit of the dead child that they had before, so no problemo! <i>Long discussions about being able to 'walk the sleep' only during menses or while bleeding for another reason?</i> Never mind, here's a small child doing it without precocious puberty or signs of abuse. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Fifthly, there seemed to be more <b>posturing</b> between our male characters (namely, Finnikin and any other male he meets along the way) than I have seen since middle school. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380382072i/739590._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It was getting a bit ridiculous. The number of times Finnikin charges someone, has a fight (without any physical consequences EVER!) - just to become their BFF afterwards was getting too much to count.<br><br>Anyway, I was more than willing to overlook the flaws - I do that all the time, in the countless books that I love. But with this one, I just could not. <br>In <i>11/22/63</i> (a perfect example of a book I loved enough to forgive all kinds of flaws), Stephen King quotes a Japanese proverb that apparently goes, <i>"If there is love, smallpox scars are as pretty as dimples."</i> Well, with no love all I see is smallpox scars. <b>2.5 stars.</b><br>----------------------<br><b>
  <i>Sorry, book, I will be walking into the sunset alone. Without you by my side. It was not meant to be, Finnikin.</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380382072i/739591.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6389399312093673524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1205731368" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1205731368" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1205731368?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763643614" href="/book/show/6719736-finnikin-of-the-rock">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1205731368" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16145102844364707958">Trying to rate this book has me pulling at my hair. It’s hard. So hard. Why is it such a difficult thing? It was fascinating, realistic and definitely well-written.<br/><br/>But before I could find it fascinating, realistic and well-written, I had to read around one hundred so-very-slow pages. <br/><br/>I think it’s amazing when a book suddenly gets better, as if some spell had been cast on us to finally see the magic of it. And on the twin bright side, I do have as feeling that I won’t have the same experience wit</span>
  <span id="freeText16145102844364707958" style="display:none">Trying to rate this book has me pulling at my hair. It’s hard. So hard. Why is it such a difficult thing? It was fascinating, realistic and definitely well-written.<br /><br />But before I could find it fascinating, realistic and well-written, I had to read around one hundred so-very-slow pages. <br /><br />I think it’s amazing when a book suddenly gets better, as if some spell had been cast on us to finally see the magic of it. And on the twin bright side, I do have as feeling that I won’t have the same experience with the next two books in the series.<br /><br />The real problem is that it took me a long time to see the characters as real people. Before the hundredth page, they were just lovely, original names on paper, nothing more. They don’t share much about themselves, and so, it was hard for me to find anything we have in common. <br /><br />But I eventually did. As the story progresses, we meet more characters who are either important to the plot or are connected somehow to the main ones. Sometimes both. These connections make Finnikin, Sir Topher and Evanjalin open up on their pasts, life experiences and fears. <br /><br />I felt somewhat out of breath when I turned the last pages; I’m not going to lie. Not because it’s rather super slow-paced and there’s quite a lot of walking done by the characters (they should learn to run sometime), but because there’s so much heartache, so much sadness, so much struggling to do the right thing. It’s exhausting at some point. But oh so very admirable and beautiful in a way. <br /><br />I commend anyone who has read this book. It isn’t easy. It’s like reading five books in one. I can only imagine how much time and effort the author has put in it. I commend her, too. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16145102844364707958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_227776023" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227776023" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227776023?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763643614" href="/book/show/6719736-finnikin-of-the-rock">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Steph by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=aussie">aussie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2012-favs">2012-favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=yeah-baby-5-stars">yeah-baby-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=action-packed">action-packed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=awesome">awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=pure-win">pure-win</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227776023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13075031991701678127">Whew. So much WIN I can hardly stand it!<br/><br/>\(^o^)/<br/><br/>Girls <b>rule</b> and boys <i>drool</i>!<br/><br/>Oh my <em>sweet</em>... just gimme the next book now!<br/><br/>First, a cavet: This review will probably be the most unhelpful review you might ever read because nothing I say will do the book justice. I'll just use this space to ramble and hopefully it makes some sort of coherency.<br/><br/>I remember the first time I heard about Melina Marchetta and her special fragrance of awesome she regularly emits whenever she publishes a novel. I had seen review</span>
  <span id="freeText13075031991701678127" style="display:none">Whew. So much WIN I can hardly stand it!<br><br>\(^o^)/<br><br>Girls <b>rule</b> and boys <i>drool</i>!<br><br>Oh my <em>sweet</em>... just gimme the next book now!<br><br>First, a cavet: This review will probably be the most unhelpful review you might ever read because nothing I say will do the book justice. I'll just use this space to ramble and hopefully it makes some sort of coherency.<br><br>I remember the first time I heard about Melina Marchetta and her special fragrance of awesome she regularly emits whenever she publishes a novel. I had seen reviews of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Jellice Road</a>, <em>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/82434.Saving_Francesca" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Saving Francesca</a>
</em>, and <em>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7417780-the-piper-s-son" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">The Piper's Son</a>
</em> popping up left and right in my GoodReads feed all proclaiming that this woman was the cat's <em>meow</em>. But still I resisted the urge to hop on the Marchetta bandwagon for whatever reason. I was the Grinch sitting comfortably on my hill watching all the citizens of Whoville fangirl.<br><br><a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/03/20120312-131618.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361946i/713024.jpg" alt="" width="300" height="260" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>Yup, that's me. Especially when writing a 1 star review.</i><br><br>Finally, my co-blogger, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Kat Kennedy</a>, shook me fiercely and demanded I get off my ass and head to my local library. Naturally, I did exactly as she said because when the Boss Lady gets bitchy, you don't ask questions. Unless, of course, you don't happen to favor your head. *shrug* Your choice. Always your choice.<br><br>So, I stared at the book when I got home and silently told myself, "This better be good or I'm going to troll the shit outta Kennedy's review." It wasn't a threat, it was a promise.<br><br>At about 15% into the book, I completely forgot about my vow to make her previous trolls look like cute bunnies.<br><br>At about 25% in, even though I checked the book out from the library, I purchased the Kindle edition for my iPad so I could read late into the night while my household slept.<br><br>At about 35% in, anyone who attempted to talk with me while I was glued to the book was met with silence or a growl. My husband made the snide remark that the iPad would be permanently affixed to my forehead if I remained in "that ridiculous reading position."<br><br><a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/03/20120312-131010.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361946i/713025.jpg" alt="" width="224" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><i>This is actually a real photo taken by my hus­band for mock­ery at a later date. Don’t worry. Vengeance will be mine!</i><br><br>At about 40% in, while at the bookstore, I raged because they didn't have Finnikin in stock. What the hell was their problem anyway?!<br><br>Somewhere between 50-100%, my husband began to worry I would run away to Australia and proclaim my love to Melina Merchetta. I won't pretend the thought didn't cross my mind.<br><br>Its been quite a long time since I added a book to my "All Time Favorites" shelf and out of all the books that reside there none ever truly came close to competing with my number one favorite: Harry Potter. Until now. Oh my god, this book was amazing!<br><br>Melina Merchetta, you humble me. This is one of the best books I have ever read. The rich world building. The realistic characters. The heartbreaking romance. You created a world I never wanted to leave.<br><br>Authors please take note. THIS is how you create a believable world, societies, and cultures. THIS is how you write a strong female character. THIS is how you show the unfair treatment of women in a society, having a heroine rise above, and yet your book still proudly waves its feminist flag. THIS is how you create memorable minor characters. THIS is how you write from a male point-of-view without him sounding like a wannabe. THIS is how you write an <strong>epic</strong> book.<br><br>Badass, Marchetta. <strong>Bad</strong><em>ass</em>.<br><br>A piece of advice from the hard-to-please, Grinch of Book-land: Read this book. It is amazing, fantastic, brilliant and everything in between. When US readers get their hands on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727-froi-of-the-exiles" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a>, and later this year <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165761-quintana-of-charyn" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Quintana of the Charyn</a> for those lucky Aussies, I'm sure GoodReads will resemble nothing short of gnats flying into the bright, blue light. And I will be proudly be one of them.<br><br>*clears throat* Now if you'll excuse me, I have a plane to catch.<br><br>So, yes this review was probably not helpful, but I hear there is a <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/2012/03/signed-giveaway-for-froi-of-the-exiles-by-melina-marchetta-and-a-finnikin-book-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">giveaway</a> for a <b>signed copy of Froi of the Exiles up on Cuddlebuggery! </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13075031991701678127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_92089994" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92089994" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92089994?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763643614" href="/book/show/6719736-finnikin-of-the-rock">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Kristin Cashore, Megan Whalen Turner</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=aus-nz">aus-nz</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92089994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer319325754442750351">As seen on <a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/post-title-click-and-type-to-edit1.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Readventurer</a><br/><br/>My second reading of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6719736.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles___1_' title='Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles, #1) by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Finnikin of the Rock</a> and I am changing my mind - 5 stars!<br/><br/>Now, when I have more fantasy under my belt to compare this book to, I am pretty confident it offers something that many others in the genre don't. This is a fantasy that is not drowned in clunky, 1000-pages long world-building, this is a book about people. People whose country is torn into pieces, people exiled from their homeland, lost, damaged, abused men, women and children. As a story of</span>
  <span id="freeText319325754442750351" style="display:none">As seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/post-title-click-and-type-to-edit1.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a><br /><br />My second reading of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6719736.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles___1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles, #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a> and I am changing my mind - 5 stars!<br /><br />Now, when I have more fantasy under my belt to compare this book to, I am pretty confident it offers something that many others in the genre don't. This is a fantasy that is not drowned in clunky, 1000-pages long world-building, this is a book about people. People whose country is torn into pieces, people exiled from their homeland, lost, damaged, abused men, women and children. As a story of a displaced, broken nation that fights to rebuild itself <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6719736.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles___1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles, #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a> is almost without a flaw. <br /><br />But of course there is more to love. All the nuances of the narrative, plot lines that make Melina's works so rich - there is a love story in which a couple struggle for the upper hand in their young relationship; there are scenes of friendship and loyalty; there are intricacies of the relationships between fathers and sons, respect, pride and competitiveness all tangled; there is a heartbreak of a love once powerful but now sullied by years of violence and abuse; there is an enemy, despicable and crass, but now not reformed but changed; there are strong men and there are even stronger women. It's hard to list it all, but Melina writes everything with such power, managing to break your heart with a sentence, a word, a glance.<br /><br />I still think the pacing could have been better though. The climax, the high point of the story, is simply too short, too understated. There is not enough feeling of a lot being at stake, it lacks danger and excitement. <br /><br />However, there are so many other things about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6719736.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles___1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles, #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a> I loved that I am happy to overlook the obvious flaws, to stick to my 5 stars and to wait for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a> with eager anticipation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="319325754442750351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_184826857" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/184826857" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/184826857?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763643614" href="/book/show/6719736-finnikin-of-the-rock">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer184826857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9758727532856959823"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Whenever I write a review of a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta' title='Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melina Marchetta</a> book, I risk sounding like the same old broken record... but, whatever, it's not my fault if she constantly manages to deliver the stuff I love! I'm not sure what'll happen if I ever dislike one of her novels, probably the sky will fall in and the world will end. Don't you know what to expect from Marchetta by now? If not, then I'll fill you in briefly: interesting, memorable and the very opposite of cliched characters, flawless writing, a plot</span>
  <span id="freeText9758727532856959823" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Whenever I write a review of a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" title="Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a> book, I risk sounding like the same old broken record... but, whatever, it's not my fault if she constantly manages to deliver the stuff I love! I'm not sure what'll happen if I ever dislike one of her novels, probably the sky will fall in and the world will end. Don't you know what to expect from Marchetta by now? If not, then I'll fill you in briefly: interesting, memorable and the very opposite of cliched characters, flawless writing, a plot that is gripping even though it isn't about supernatural creatures taking over the world (yet - but I'm actually curious to see how she'd handle that genre)... I feel confident enough to say that she is one of the very best modern writers (in any genre).<br><br>Okay... so Finnikin.<br><br>Let's just say that this year - well, the past few months - has completely changed the way I view traditional fantasy. The kind with made up worlds and magical realms, that sort of thing. In the past I just haven't cared. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lord of the Rings</a>? Wake me up when it's over. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153008.Kushiel_s_Dart__Kushiel___1_" title="Kushiel's Dart (Kushiel, #1) by Jacqueline Carey" rel="nofollow noopener">Kushiel's Dart</a>? A steaming pile of WTF. I was actually afraid to start this book a few months ago because I didn't want to face the disappointment of reading a Marchetta book that did nothing for me. But then my opinion was forever changed by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner" title="Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Whalen Turner</a> and her wonderful Queen's Thief series. This sudden change in my opinion of the fantasy genre was only solidified by reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4932435.Finnikin_of_the_Rock__Lumatere_Chronicles__1_" title="Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles #1) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a>.<br><br>It's difficult to pick a favourite character when they are all so well developed, and also difficult to pick a favourite part of the novel when it's full of some of the best-written action, adventure and romance scenes. The women kick ass and even the toughest of men have their weaknesses that only serve to endear us to them more. I've said it before and I'm sure I'll be saying it again: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" title="Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a> never <i>ever</i> wastes characters. They are all important to the novel, nobody is a throwaway.<br><br>There is no such thing as a perfect novel and certain parts could have been slightly improved - like the climax - but this is about as close as it gets. I'm even more of a Marchetta fan after reading this than I was before. Now I just have to sit and sulk until I get my hands on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a>.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9758727532856959823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572638169p2/2016128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90414336?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763643614" href="/book/show/6719736-finnikin-of-the-rock">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=forgot-to-drink-the-kool-aid">forgot-to-drink-the-kool-aid</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=color-blue">color-blue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=color-red">color-red</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=australian-authors">australian-authors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90414336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4572437448015599714"><b>I think this is the point where Marchetta and I go our separate ways.</b> I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178284243' rel='nofollow noopener'>Saving Francesca</a> and didn't enjoy it, and thought maybe it was just my aversion to realistic/contemporary fiction that was keeping me from riding the Marchetta love-train. After this second attempt I think she's just not for me. <b>There isn't one thing I can point out that makes me say "this" is why I don't like her books, but there are numerous problems I can draw attention to.</b><br/><br/><b>My biggest gripe is that the plot hinges on </b></span>
  <span id="freeText4572437448015599714" style="display:none"><b>I think this is the point where Marchetta and I go our separate ways.</b> I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178284243" rel="nofollow noopener">Saving Francesca</a> and didn't enjoy it, and thought maybe it was just my aversion to realistic/contemporary fiction that was keeping me from riding the Marchetta love-train. After this second attempt I think she's just not for me. <b>There isn't one thing I can point out that makes me say "this" is why I don't like her books, but there are numerous problems I can draw attention to.</b><br /><br /><b>My biggest gripe is that the plot hinges on assumptions made by numerous characters.</b> What I mean by this is: if Evanjalin had revealed her secret early on then a lot of the problems that cropped up wouldn't have manifested. Although, Marchetta does address this by having one of the characters point out to Finnikin that if he knew the truth then he wouldn’t have made the right choices. So we have assumptions on top of assumptions now. Evanjalin constantly keeps secrets from them: both big and small ones. She puts <i>everyone</i> on a need to know basis, and makes their journey harder by doing so. I can’t even count how many times I wanted to shake her and tell her just to be straight with them. It was beyond frustrating.<br /><br />And THEN, when her secret is revealed, everyone treats Evanjalin like she’s a saint and did no wrong-doing; suddenly, she's up on this pedestal and can't be touched. This felt so manufactured and inorganic. Everyone acts differently and practically out-of-character from how they were just a few chapters ago. I can understand some of this <i>to a point</i>, but the complete 180 everyone did just didn't sit well with me. Surprisingly, Finnikin was the only one who still acted marginally the same.<br /><br /><b>Evanjalin manipulates everyone and everything around her, without any regret.</b> She is largely of the mind that "the ends justify the means" and does whatever the hell she wants. Evanjalin knows best and everyone else can just suck it. I understand she went through more than any person should have to endure, but her actions and her attitude throughout the book did not endear me to her. <b>I liked Finnikin until he decided that he was in love with Evanjalin</b>; which was yet another thing that didn’t occur naturally. Evanjalin lies, manipulates, and somewhat betrays everyone in her traveling party, even Finnikin, and everyone just accepts this and falls in love with her. It's so mind-boggling. <br /><br /><b>Then we have Froi.</b> I will never get over what he did, and I honestly don't understand why Marchetta had his character do what he did, because it didn't fit with the image she created of him for the rest of the book. You want me to like him? Well, don’t make him <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[attempt to rape the main character. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I don’t care what sort of environment someone grows up in, I can't imagine anyone <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[being able to rehabilitate, forgive, and grow to love someone who tried to rape them. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Then there are two nit-picky things that were always in the back of my head.</b> Finnikin learns the Yut language within a few days. And, from what I gather, the Yut language is very different from any of the other languages, as it’s described as being guttural and full of grunts (166), so it’s not like it’s just a dialect of another language or even a close sister-language. <b>Finnikin is also a wiz when it comes to learning new languages, and I understand that, but to be able to make complex proclamations in a language you’ve only been taught in a matter of days is incredibly implausible.</b><br /><br /><b>Also, we have the multiple races</b> (different skin/eye/hair color combinations are constantly remarked on) <b>all living on one tiny island.</b> There is a reason that almost 99% of the people in Japan are Japanese (even taking into account their tendency towards xenophobia). You just won't find so many different ethnicities living on such a small land mass, and even if this did somehow exist, they would eventually interbreed to the point where everyone would be a mix of everyone else. And, considering the remark Trevanion makes about the Yuts being at war for the past 10,000 years (175), this makes the fact that there are so many races even more unbelievable. And why are the people who live in the hot tropical climates fair-skinned with pale eyes (171)? The closer you are to the sun, the darker you’ll be in order to survive. This is such a weird thing to overlook.<br /><br /><b>I also felt like the magic and religion of this world were thrown together rather haphazardly.</b> Nothing is really explained all that much and you’re just supposed to accept things for what they are. I don't mind not having info dumps about everything, but at least <i>eventually</i> let me into the club so I know what the rules are. Evanjalin explains <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that she can walk the sleep when she bleeds (which we later find out that she can do this if the wound is self-inflicted as well), does that mean that Vestie walks the sleep somehow in a different way? Obviously a toddler isn’t going to have a period, and no one would deliberately cut her, so how did she manage it? Why go to the trouble of creating this situation for Evanjalin and then arbitrarily change the rules when Vestie is introduced? Did I miss something in the explanation? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And the religion seemed pointless as well, when it didn't even factor into anything other than having a place to sequester people. I didn’t understand placing so much emphasis on Sagrami and Lagrami worshippers, other than to have a convenient group of people to persecute.<br /><br /><b>Marchetta is a competent writer, but I don’t think she’s a good story-teller.</b> There are too many things I can pick at and too many issues I have with her characters that I just find myself unable to enjoy her books as a whole. This is likely my last chance I'm giving her, because I normally like fantasy so much more than contemporary, and this one had almost as many issues for me as Francesca did. <b>I know lots of people love Marchetta, but in this book lots of people love Evanjalin too, and I think in both instances I'm just not drinking the right Kool-aid.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4572437448015599714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11547918350055320338" style="display:none">This is not a review. This is a <s>badly written</s> poem.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Then I choose to drown,” Finnikin said. “In hope. Rather than float into nothing.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Since I was a nipper I have come to the conclusion<br />That when it comes to fantasy: I am strongly opposed. <br />When I read a book with long, confusing names<br />And swords and maps, its pages remain closed. <br />So imagine my surprise when I finished <i>this</i> one<br />(In the early hours of this morning, I feel I should note)<br />That my stomach was rumbling (I had no time to eat!)<br />And my heart was in my throat.<br />A tale of hopeful heroes, sacrifice and loss<br />History, homeland and prophecies told, <br />Of faraway lands, identity and faith<br />And love and flower fields of gold.<br />I learnt a lot from the tale of Finn and his friends<br />Like how to remain fierce in a threadbare smock<br />And how to fight thieves and how to hold a sword<br />(FYI: Similar to how you’d hold a….*cough*)<br />MM’s heroes are not made of puppy dog tails<br />And they don’t mope around being rude<br />It appears you <i>can</i> be a great character (and get the girl)<br />Without being in a permanent mood. <br />They are complex, compelling and always <s>sexy</s> brave,<br />And they treat their chosen one like an equal <s>except Will</s>.<br />From Jonah to Mackee to good old <s>Trevanion</s> Finn.<br />(On Froi, the jury is out ‘til the sequel) <br />But this book isn’t about the boys for the ladies are the ones to watch<br />With their passion and love and their unrelenting loyalty<br />And determination to show they will fight for what’s right<br />From the goddesses to the lost ones and, of course, the royalty. <br /><br />But it’s easy to see, from my other reviews, that I am smitten<br />With every single book that Ms Marchetta has written. <br />And it’s safe to say that if her next book was about<br />Broody boys who are mean and think it’s sexy to shout<br />Or crying girls and fairies and triangles of love<br />Vampires and angling or all of the above.<br />Even if it was called “<i>The Mating Habits of Eels</i>” <br />Or “<i>Puppies Aren’t Just For Christmas: 100 Delicious Meals</i>”<br />I’d still read it and laugh and swoon and cry <br />And then place a copy in the hands of my friends and say<br />“<i>You need to give this a try</i>.”<br /><br /><i>I received a copy of this book from the author. </i><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16640711120468356144">Yeah thank you <i>very much</i> Melina Marchetta for the <b>biggest lump in my throat <i>for hours</i></b> on end reading this. People say the word 'slow burn'. This wasn't particularly slow but by god, it BURNED!! <br/>It burned <b>bad.</b><br/><br/>I was not prepared for the overwhelming emotions I'd feel for the characters & this Kingdom. Despite glowing reviews from many trusted gr friends, somehow I still underestimated the effect this book would have on me. Maybe it had to do with the fact I'd never read anything by her before but </span>
  <span id="freeText16640711120468356144" style="display:none">Yeah thank you <i>very much</i> Melina Marchetta for the <b>biggest lump in my throat <i>for hours</i></b> on end reading this. People say the word 'slow burn'. This wasn't particularly slow but by god, it BURNED!! <br>It burned <b>bad.</b><br><br>I was not prepared for the overwhelming emotions I'd feel for the characters &amp; this Kingdom. Despite glowing reviews from many trusted gr friends, somehow I still underestimated the effect this book would have on me. Maybe it had to do with the fact I'd never read anything by her before but either way,<b> I was floored. </b><br><br><b>
  <i>So much courage, so much love. <br>Such hope and unity.</i>
</b><br><br>Lumaterans were scattered. They were destitute. They were exiles. Yet there was always this sense of togetherness, <i>belongingness.</i><br>And gosh it was fucking magical!<br><br>I needed to conciously holding back my tears when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Froi relay Evanjalin's supposed last wish to Finnikin <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481541393ra/21429920.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br> I know. I remember this particular scene :<br><blockquote>"sheep shit" <br><i>Bastard</i>
</blockquote><br>^I love the friendship between Finnikin &amp; Lucian (lol)<br><br><br>rating: ★★★★½<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_558042434" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/558042434" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer791780407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2654013609076594850">12/07/16 Kindle deal today for 1.99 <a href='https://www.amazon.com/dp/B003EINO58/ref=as_li_ss_il?_encoding=UTF8&colid=17Z7480K6AD4D&coliid=I21Z7L7UB0QSV8&linkCode=li1&tag=rabrea-20&linkId=015cd56256f3a4fb0d271d520e2b231c' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a> <br/><br/><b>Buddy Read/Re-read with a great group of people at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-lumatere-chronicles-group-read' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lumatere Chronicles Group Read</a> starting with Finnikin on Dec 1 2015</b><br/><br/>So wonderful, the second time trough I loved it more so I'm bumping the rating up to 4.5 stars.<br/><br/>I laughed, cried and was just amazed by the complexity of the characters in the story Marchetta tells.<br/><a href='http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/finnquote_zps0a13f6fb.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418007984i/12635351.jpg' alt=' photo finnquote_zps0a13f6fb.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/><b>Original Review Dec 2013</b><br/><br/>4.5 Stars<br/><br/>Finnikin of the Rock was so much better than I expected. I thought it would be about Finnikin and it is but</span>
  <span id="freeText2654013609076594850" style="display:none">12/07/16 Kindle deal today for 1.99 <a href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/B003EINO58/ref=as_li_ss_il?_encoding=UTF8&amp;colid=17Z7480K6AD4D&amp;coliid=I21Z7L7UB0QSV8&amp;linkCode=li1&amp;tag=rabrea-20&amp;linkId=015cd56256f3a4fb0d271d520e2b231c" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> <br><br><b>Buddy Read/Re-read with a great group of people at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-lumatere-chronicles-group-read" rel="nofollow noopener">Lumatere Chronicles Group Read</a> starting with Finnikin on Dec 1 2015</b><br><br>So wonderful, the second time trough I loved it more so I'm bumping the rating up to 4.5 stars.<br><br>I laughed, cried and was just amazed by the complexity of the characters in the story Marchetta tells.<br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/finnquote_zps0a13f6fb.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418007984i/12635351.jpg" alt=" photo finnquote_zps0a13f6fb.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><b>Original Review Dec 2013</b><br><br>4.5 Stars<br><br>Finnikin of the Rock was so much better than I expected. I thought it would be about Finnikin and it is but the character that really stole the show for me was Evanjalin. If you like fantasies with strong heroic characters that fumble along the way then this book is right up your ally. It is another very well done YA fantasy novel that is smart and intricate enough to be for adults but face paced enough to appeal to YA as well. The world is intricate, the lore well thought out and the overall story line was fantastic.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Balthazar pledged to die defending his royal house of Lumuatere. Finnikin swore to be their protector and guide for as long as he lived. Lucian vowed he would be the light whom they traveled toward in times of need.”</i>
</b><br><br>There are too many characters and so much going on throughout the story that it is hard to give a good detailed review. So I will do my best to just give a generalized one. The Royal family of the Lumineers was slaughtered and an Imposter King sits on the throne. A witch put a curse on the land when the people turned against her religion and since that day some of the Kingdom was trapped inside the walls of the curse while others were trapped outside and cannot enter. It is thought that perhaps the son of the king Balthazar might have gone into hiding and still be alive years later. Evanjalin is a mystic of sorts and convinces Finnikin it is his quest to help her return a king to their people and help them break the curse and so our quest begins.<br><br>It seems like Evanjalin is playing by a set of rules no one else can knows and right away it is unclear if she is a force of good or bad, but it is certain she is a force to be reckoned with. To be able to convince the exiles of Lumineer to journey back to their kingdom they must rescue the former Captain of the Guard and find the men of the Lost Guard to help them.<br><br><b>
  <i>“There are worse things than a lie and there are better things than the truth!”</i>
</b><br><br>There is a slow burning romance that is building between Evanjalin and Finnikin. He is torn because she is complex and intricate and wants so much from him and as far as he knows she might be promised to the Balthazar if they ever find him. But he can’t deny that what he feels for her he has never felt for another. Their moments together good and bad made the story all the better.<br><br><b>
  <i>""Is she not the smartest girl in the land?"<br>"And the biggest liar and the most unpredictable" Perri Muttered."</i>
</b><br><br>This is full of mystery, action, adventure and hope. I was enthralled after the first few chapters and couldn’t walk away from the story. There are many hints along the way and I really wanted to find out if my theories were right. Some definitely were and others were not but the culmination of the story of a peoples journey home was an epic tale. <br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/Finnhands_zps50a39e81.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418007984i/12635352.jpg" alt=" photo Finnhands_zps50a39e81.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>There are sweet moments, horrifying moments and moments of the greatest hope. I can’t wait to read more from this world in the next book Froi and the Exiles. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="2654013609076594850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1724607460" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1724607460" />
    <a title="Sana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26402455-sana"><img alt="Sana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560612398p2/26402455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1724607460?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sana" href="/user/show/26402455-sana">Sana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780763652920" href="/book/show/10636358-finnikin-of-the-rock">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">High Fantasy lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=i-dont-get-the-hype">i-dont-get-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=shawty-so-bad">shawty-so-bad</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1724607460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12972826657184497019">3.5 stars. <br/><br/><b>This book put me in a slump.</b> I've been reading this since January 9, 2017 and it is now January 29, 2017. This wasn't a <i>bad</i> book. It's fun and enjoyable, but I, however, wasn't able to enjoy it because I was dragging this book for almost an entire month. I think I kind of forgot what happened in the beginning, whoops. <br/><br/>This was my first High Fantasy read and I can successfully say, I enjoyed it. It wasn't anything original, typical, my-kingdom-has-fallen-and-someone-claims-the-real-kin</span>
  <span id="freeText12972826657184497019" style="display:none">3.5 stars. <br /><br /><b>This book put me in a slump.</b> I've been reading this since January 9, 2017 and it is now January 29, 2017. This wasn't a <i>bad</i> book. It's fun and enjoyable, but I, however, wasn't able to enjoy it because I was dragging this book for almost an entire month. I think I kind of forgot what happened in the beginning, whoops. <br /><br />This was my first High Fantasy read and I can successfully say, I enjoyed it. It wasn't anything original, typical, my-kingdom-has-fallen-and-someone-claims-the-real-king-is-alive-so-off-we-go-to-revive-the-kingdom. So off goes Evanjalin, Sir Tropher, and Finnkin in hopes of finding their king and claiming back their land. <br /><br />I would be lying if I said I loved this. I really wanted to, but this thing called a fucking slump made it impossible for me to enjoy anything. I didn't hate this, hence the 3.5 stars. The world building, imo, was great. There were so many different kingdoms, languages etc etc and it was really fun to read and learn about. <br /><br />I loved all the characters. I know many people found Evanjalin annoying, but imo, she was badass and full of surprises. She's not your typical weak heroine (though sometimes she cried too much), she's strong, clever, and she is just #goals. Okay? Okay. Tbh, like I probably mentioned before, I kind of forgot things while reading this so I'm not sure if there is anything special about Finnikin. To me, he was a bland and boring character. I felt like the author didn't describe much about him, despite the fact that the entire story is told from his view in third person. He was okay, but extremely bland and boring. <br /><br /><b>Froi</b> is my son and I love him sm and I can't wait to read his story. And I apologize for the shitty review guys. <br /><br />Overall, this was an interesting experience and I'm pretty sure High Fantasy people will love this. Give it a try, I'm sure it won't disappoint. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12972826657184497019" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1260097824604090480">I'm really emotional don't toUCH ME.<br/><br/>This was so SOOOO good. It was a little overhyped for me (I blame you, heist crew friends) but I really enjoyed it besides that. I loved the characters, even though they frustrated the HECK out of me sometimes, and even though some of their decisions felt more like plot devices than actual decisions people would make. <br/>This book takes a little bit to actually get going and took me about 100 pages to fully get into it, but when it gets good it gets so good.<br/>I WAS</span>
  <span id="freeText1260097824604090480" style="display:none">I'm really emotional don't toUCH ME.<br /><br />This was so SOOOO good. It was a little overhyped for me (I blame you, heist crew friends) but I really enjoyed it besides that. I loved the characters, even though they frustrated the HECK out of me sometimes, and even though some of their decisions felt more like plot devices than actual decisions people would make. <br />This book takes a little bit to actually get going and took me about 100 pages to fully get into it, but when it gets good it gets so good.<br />I WAS SO EMOTIONAL A LOT OF THE TIME LIKE HOW CAN THIS BOOK MAKE ME SO EMOTIONAL WITH LIKE 5 PAGES OF BACK STORY. Idk. But that was its shining glorious light - the emotions it made me feel SO MANY.<br />Overall, I wasn't super blown away but I still loved it.<br />Also wanna say CALLED IT from almost the beginning and if you read the book you'll probably know what I mean. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/998997406?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780763652920" href="/book/show/10636358-finnikin-of-the-rock">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=your-mileage-may-vary">your-mileage-may-vary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=wallowing-in-misery-and-angst">wallowing-in-misery-and-angst</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer998997406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7959437169398851848"><b>Initial post:</b> A weak 4 stars from me. I liked a lot of things about this story, but I have Issues.<br/><br/><b>Six months later:</b> Well, I should have written a full review a long time ago. At this point, all my efforts to gather my thoughts about this book have just resulted in something all stream-of-consciousness, namely this:<br/><br/>"man, this is taking a long time to get going and it's all depressing and angsty and I can't even with all this grimness and death ugh why does this person think she's so cool seriousl</span>
  <span id="freeText7959437169398851848" style="display:none"><b>Initial post:</b> A weak 4 stars from me. I liked a lot of things about this story, but I have Issues.<br><br><b>Six months later:</b> Well, I should have written a full review a long time ago. At this point, all my efforts to gather my thoughts about this book have just resulted in something all stream-of-consciousness, namely this:<br><br>"man, this is taking a long time to get going and it's all depressing and angsty and I can't even with all this grimness and death ugh why does this person think she's so cool seriously annoying me with all her secrets that she can't tell just because wait WHAT?!? why would you even keep an attempted rapist around why are people so stupid okay this is getting pretty good FINALLY."<br><br>So probably 3 1/2 stars for me, and in retrospect I've decided to round down my rating. I wasn't that excited about it, and I'm not motivated to read the sequel(s). But I'm an outlier here; most of my friends loved this, so just ignore me sitting in the corner here muttering darkly.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434042196i/15170454._SX540_.jpg" width="293" height="235" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
