    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_138870781" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138870781" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138870781?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8757361-finnikin-of-the-rock">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=male-approved">male-approved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=great-books">great-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=beloved">beloved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=aussie-and-nz">aussie-and-nz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=once-upon-a-time">once-upon-a-time</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=rereading-material">rereading-material</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138870781" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9781168901435621065">------- 2019<br/><br/>8 years ago I was enjoying for the first time one of the most astonishing stories I've come across so far and the best fantasy series in the bookish world... if I say so myself. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/p/BPkfaPHg71t/' rel='nofollow noopener'> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485285998i/21801074.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></a><br/><br/>A story of great loss, of curses and anguish, but also hope.<br/>A story with the strongest characters in front and the brightest author behind. <br/>A story that takes my breath away each time I re-read it, one that sings to my heart and fills me with such ineffable emotion.<br/><br/>Finnikin of the Rock is the beginning of a </span>
  <span id="freeText9781168901435621065" style="display:none">------- 2019<br><br>8 years ago I was enjoying for the first time one of the most astonishing stories I've come across so far and the best fantasy series in the bookish world... if I say so myself. <br><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/p/BPkfaPHg71t/" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1485285998i/21801074.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>A story of great loss, of curses and anguish, but also hope.<br>A story with the strongest characters in front and the brightest author behind. <br>A story that takes my breath away each time I re-read it, one that sings to my heart and fills me with such ineffable emotion.<br><br>Finnikin of the Rock is the beginning of a journey, but it's so perfectly defined and refined, it's hard to believe that all that development takes just one book. And as fascinating and intricately woven the magical plot is, just to wait for the next 2 books to see how much more magnificent Marchetta's mind can be... <br><br>It might break your heart, it might chill you to the bone, it might fill you with despair, but also glee... and I assure you that it <i>will</i> all be well worth it - because Lumatere Chronicles is one story of a kind!<br><br><blockquote>
  <br>
  <i>Book description:<br><br>At the age of nine, Finnikin's world is shattered by the five days of the unspeakable: the royal family of Lumatere is brutally murdered, an imposter seizes the throne, and a curse binds all who remain inside the kingdom's walls. Those who escape are left to roam as exiles. <br><br>Ten years later, Finnikin and his mentor, Sir Topher, are summoned to meet Evanjalin, a young novice with a startling claim: Balthazar, the heir to the throne of Lumatere and Finnikin's childhood friend, is alive, and she can lead Finnikin to him. Even as he suspects this arrogant young woman, Finnikin also begins to believe that Lumatere might one day be raised.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>-------2011<br><br>Wonderful, amazing, beautiful, absolutely brilliant... I need more stars! ★★★★★★★★★★<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/finnikin-of-the-rock.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380343563i/698927.jpg" width="400" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <i>"Because without our language, we have lost ourselves. Who are we without our words?" </i>
</blockquote><br>This was such a powerful story that got straight to my heart. After finishing it I was left speechless - Melina Marchetta has this effect on people. The characters are so well defined, the story is so complex... All that I've felt while reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road" title="On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Jellicoe Road</a> I felt again while reading this book, and these 2 stories are nothing alike. <br><br><b>What I liked</b><br>It is hard to tell because there are so many things on this list, I would never finish - I liked the storyline, the characters, their evolution, the description, the twists in the story, and the ending (that precious ending - it was perfect). To keep it short: it was an emotional roller-coaster and it felt so good.<br><br><b>What I liked, but it was not really to like</b><br>The world described in this story - all that suffering of the people in exile and the ones trapped in the kingdom - it was heartbreaking. It hurt to know what happened (during those "5 days of the unspeakable" and after that), it was absolutely cruel, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ and knowing what Evanjalin felt that each time she walked through those people's sleep was unbearable. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>What I didn't like</b><br>Scratch this ... what was not to like?<br><br>Judging by the other books from this author I had one fear - I thought that the beginning was supposed to be slow, but that was not the case.. I found it rather interesting and full of events from the very first page and this was a very pleasant surprise. This is definitely one of my favorite books and I can't wait for the sequel (even though it was so beautiful and perfect that I didn't feel the need to see what happens next )<br><br><a href="http://untroubledheart.deviantart.com/art/there-is-always-hope-263218562" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380343563i/698928.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Characters &amp; favorite quotes:<br><br><b>- Finnikin</b><br>I am starting with him because he is the main character and the reason for all 416 pages of <i>"the story, as told to those not born to see such days, recorded in the book of Lumatere so they will never forget."</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>Balthazar pledged to die defending his royal house of Lumatere. Finnikin swore to be their protector and guide for as long as he lived. Lucian vowed he would be the light whom they traveled toward in times of need.</i><br><br><b>- Evanjalin</b><br>A young novice that in the beginning does not tell as much, but as the story unfolds there are no words enough to express all that she holds inside, all that she had lived in those 10 years since the "five days of the unspeakable". Also she is the best female character I've read about in a while.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>- "It takes great character to handle Evanjalin and Froi," Finnikin went on. "You would have much to fear."<br>- "What is the worst that can happen?" Aldron scoffed.<br>- "She could have you imprisoned in the mines. Or sell you to the slave traders of Sorel," Finnikin said with a shrug.</i><br><br><b>- Sir Topher</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>Let's accept our path, Finnikin, and hold our tongue, as the novice does so beautifully.</i><br><br><b>- Froi</b> <br>Looking back, I didn't know what to make of him in the first book, but just wait for the next ones, there's so much to him that doesn't meet the eye.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>"You never do anything stupid like that again," she whispered with fury. "You could have been killed, you idiot boy. It's part of your bond that I give instructions, not you."<br>Froi mumbled, and Perri leaned closer to listen. "That's very rude, Froi. And quite impossible for her to do with a bond."</i><br><br><b>- Trevanion </b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>"Finn, listen!" Trevanion said, his voice raw. "I prayed to see you one more time. It's all I prayed for. Nothing more. And my prayers were answered. Go east, I'll lead them west."<br>"We have a dilemma, then," Finnikin said fiercely. "Because I prayed that you would grow old and hold my children in your arms as you held me. My prayers have not been answered yet, Trevanion. So whose prayer is more worthy? Yours or mine?"</i><br><br>------------<br><br>My favorite moment in the book:<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396274066i/9108998.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <i>" Do you think you should warn him that I'm going to kiss you?"<br>He loved the flush that appeared on her face, and there was an intake of breath from the girls.<br>"Aldron," she said, clearing her throat, "if he agrees to become king, I'm going to let him kiss me. Please don't stop him."<br>Aldron thought for a moment and sighed, holding up his hand. "Wait there and do not move," he ordered Finnikin, before calling out to one of the other guards who stood on the platform. "Ask Perri if he's allowed to touch her if he's agreed to be king." </i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380313075i/688704.jpg" alt="" width="361" height="116" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>This review can be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/finnikin-of-the-rock.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a></i> <br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br><br><br>Later Edit:<br>Re-read in May 2013<br>I might write soon a new review for the series, as it blew my mind once more and I still love it to pieces. Just know that this is a heartbreaking story that I will always hold close to my heart. Absolutely fabulous!!!<br><br>-----<br>Re-read, Jan 2016<br><br>Lumatere Chronicles is my top favorite fantasy - one of the best series I have ever read; and it's so complex and twisted, it breaks my heart and it puts it back together again and again. <br>And so I've made my husband read it (he only reads technical stuff). And it doesn't matter that he was with this terrible cold and nothing else to do, he enjoyed it, we talked about it, and for some reason this makes me so damn happy and giddy.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137641906" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137641906?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lora" href="/user/show/4632071-lora">Lora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763643614" href="/book/show/6719736-finnikin-of-the-rock">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of YA fantasy and/or Melina Marchetta</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=lib-read">lib-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=aussies-rock-my-world">aussies-rock-my-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=quality-ya-fic">quality-ya-fic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137641906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17178060596727431470">Often times, when an author is highly talented in their genre, they don't do as well when trying their hand at another. Especially when the two genres in question are as dissimilar as realism and fantasy. Naturally, this sort of thing isn't a problem for an author like Melina Marchetta. As if being the fan proclaimed Queen of YA realistic fiction wasn't enough, she had to go and write <i>Finnikin of the Rock</i> and prove to her fans and critics alike that labels and genres mean nothing to her, that sh</span>
  <span id="freeText17178060596727431470" style="display:none">Often times, when an author is highly talented in their genre, they don't do as well when trying their hand at another. Especially when the two genres in question are as dissimilar as realism and fantasy. Naturally, this sort of thing isn't a problem for an author like Melina Marchetta. As if being the fan proclaimed Queen of YA realistic fiction wasn't enough, she had to go and write <i>Finnikin of the Rock</i> and prove to her fans and critics alike that labels and genres mean nothing to her, that she's in the top tier no matter what the task calls for. Bravo, Marchetta. Bravo.<br /><br />In the land of Skuldenore, there is a kingdom called Lumatere. Like all kingdoms, there is a King and Queen who rule over its people. These people and their rulers were happy until the day when a neighboring kingdom's rulers decided to use Lumatere as the means to eventually take over another kingdom, Belegonia. This leads to the slaughter of the King and Queen and their heirs, and soon after they are replaced by an imposter king and the majority of Lumatere's people become exiles. This is the ground work for what promises to be an epic fantasy saga.<br /><br />I can't say that I expected anything less than a remarkable male lead from Marchetta (especially after recently meeting Jonah Griggs in another one of Marchetta's masterpieces, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road" title="On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Jellicoe Road</a>), but Finnikin still took me by surprise. I imagine it is very different and probably much more difficult to write a character in a fantasy world than in the real world, and for this reason I was curious to see how Finnikin would compare to Marchetta's other male characters. It turns<br />out that he is just as brilliantly crafted as his competition. He feels envy, lust, and rage, just as any human does. But those emotions are equally matched by his level of compassion, endurance, and love for his father, his homeland, and one lucky lady.<br />And what a lady Evanjalin is! She stirs the blood of the hopeless exiles and gets them on their feet and fighting. She carries a heavy burden, of which is unbeknownst to the reader for most of the novel, but she is resolute in her quest to restore the kingdom of Lumatere. I always appreciate characters who make you want to stand up and right the wrongs in the world, and Evanjalin's fierce determination did just that for me.<br /><br />Because of her fabulous and utterly realistic portrayals of human life, Marchetta has garnered a legion of the most devoted fans an author could ask for. And I am proud to say that I'm among them. I'll be perilously balanced on the edge of my seat until the release of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a>.<br /><br />P.S. If you'd like some snippets of info on Froi's book to tide you over until its release, check out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/1531015-froi-of-the-exiles" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/1607995-2-october-2011-froi-finnikin-and-point-of-view-don-t-read-on-if-you" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17178060596727431470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1010007219" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1010007219" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1010007219?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=likeable-mc">likeable-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=knots-in-my-stomach">knots-in-my-stomach</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=autobuy-authors">autobuy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1010007219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13176957403998793945"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422146939i/13462580._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>4 stars - 4.5 stars - 5 stars?</b> <i>Oh, well, I don't know people. Sorry.</i><br/><br/><i>Finnikin of the Rock</i> is the story of people who try to step forward, and forward, and forward... Until perhaps, one day, perhaps they'll share a land called home again.<br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>"<i>Speak</i>, Finnikin wanted to shout at her. <i>Lay blame. Shout. Rage. Rage!</i>"</blockquote>
</b> <br/><i>Ready to travel with me?</i><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422146939i/13462581._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><u><i>Finnikin of the Rock</i> is <b>a journey</b></u>. The journey of Lumatere people who struggle to survive after their exile. I'll be honest, I didn't expect it to move me so much -</span>
  <span id="freeText13176957403998793945" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422146939i/13462580._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>4 stars - 4.5 stars - 5 stars?</b> <i>Oh, well, I don't know people. Sorry.</i><br><br><i>Finnikin of the Rock</i> is the story of people who try to step forward, and forward, and forward... Until perhaps, one day, perhaps they'll share a land called home again.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"<i>Speak</i>, Finnikin wanted to shout at her. <i>Lay blame. Shout. Rage. Rage!</i>"</blockquote>
</b> <br><i>Ready to travel with me?</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422146939i/13462581._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u><i>Finnikin of the Rock</i> is <b>a journey</b></u>. The journey of Lumatere people who struggle to survive after their exile. I'll be honest, I didn't expect it to move me so much - and yeah, I realized pretty fast what a fool I'd been to underestimate Melina Marchetta's ability to take my heart and squeeze it. <i>Hard</i>. <br><br><i>The fact is, I'm always fooled in the same way with this author : I'm travelling through her words, confident, conceited even, until I come across a sentence which breaks my heart. Repeatedly.</i><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"Men who in Lumatere had voices loud and passionate, who provided for their families and were respected in their villages. Now they sat in silence and relied on their children to translate for them as if they were helpless babes. Finnikin wondered what it did to a man who once stood proud. How could he pass on his stories without a language?"</blockquote>
</b> <br>There's a lot of talking in this book but it never bothered me. <i>Why?</i> Because as Sir Topher expresses it, stories and languages and well, <i>talking</i> are links we don't want to destroy. They're bonding, history, <i>
  <b>family</b>
</i>.<br><br><b>People of Lumatere are going through all the trials refugee have to face</b>. Yes that's fantasy, <b>yet their suffering sounds so real and reminds me so much of what happens near every one of our houses I got chills.</b> Sadly, I don't think there's a country in the world which doesn't have its refugee, somehow, and yeah, sure, we could argue that their country didn't disappear magically like Lumatere - no, war and poverty and corruption and selfishness did it. I'm not sure it isn't worst. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"You are evil," he seeted.<br>"Oh, the way that word is thrown around!" she said. "Everything is evil that humans can't control or conquer."</blockquote>
</b> <br>In addition to the necessity to forget their own language, entire families find themselves scattered throughout the kingdoms closed to Lumatere after the disappearance of their home. <i>Desperate. Abused. Threatened. <b>Hopeless</b>.</i> <br><br><b>Cursed.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422146939i/13462582._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There's so much to say about the <b>plot</b> and yet I'm feeling as I've already said too much. The only thing you need to know is this : following Finnikin, Evanjelin, Sir Topher and all the other *cough* Froi! *cough* has been a meaningful experience for me and I can only hope you'll feel even a glimmer of the emotion I felt. <br><br>As per usual with Melina Marchetta, <b>the characterization is flawless.</b> Really, I'm in awe of this author for her ability to create characters so <i>real</i>. Far from perfect. Both loveable and detestable. <b>Each and every one of them found the path to my heart, each in their own way.</b> Although I can be annoyed by their doubts <i>(yes Finnikin, I'm totally staring at you - but yes, I still love you)</i>, amused by their repartee, in love with their courage, frightened for them - and sometimes, by them, they can make me feel restless, proud, mad, confused - <br><br>If I you ask me to tell you <i>
  <b>one thing</b>
</i> about them, it'd be that <b>they never <i>ever</i> leave me indifferent.</b> <br> <br>Finally, what can I say about the <b>writing</b> apart from repeating how beautiful it is? I always trusted Melina Marchetta to create complex and so dynamic characters. Now I know she can also deliver <b>full-detailed settings</b>. Indeed her words resonate within us, mesmerizing, alternating between descriptions full of details and short sentences when the action requires it. <br><br><i>Well</i>, I think that's pretty clear that I loved this book, even if in some parts I felt a bit lost and wavering, especially in the third part which was a bit anticlimatic. But then, in my opinion no book is perfect, and I enjoyed so much this journey I can't hold a grudge.<br><br>I'll let you with this quote - <br><b>
  <blockquote>"Perhaps they would act as a deterrent. He could not believe anyone who heard such stories of wickedness would allow it to happen again."</blockquote>
</b> <br><i>Oh dear Finnikin, if you knew...</i><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2126608321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15137710006687766220">If I expected the book to be as good as I’d thought it would be after I couldn’t even finish reading the blurb because it was just too boring, it was probably my fault.<br/><br/>Except!! NOT!! Because the devil recommended this book to me and I wouldn’t have had to suffer through this if it weren’t for her.<br/><br/>Anyways.<br/><br/>My first complaint out of many is that <b>this book was WAY. TOO. LONG</b>. When I was at page 200, I wanted it to end right then and there, “it” meaning both the book and my life. Usually 200-paged bo</span>
  <span id="freeText15137710006687766220" style="display:none">If I expected the book to be as good as I’d thought it would be after I couldn’t even finish reading the blurb because it was just too boring, it was probably my fault.<br /><br />Except!! NOT!! Because the devil recommended this book to me and I wouldn’t have had to suffer through this if it weren’t for her.<br /><br />Anyways.<br /><br />My first complaint out of many is that <b>this book was WAY. TOO. LONG</b>. When I was at page 200, I wanted it to end right then and there, “it” meaning both the book and my life. Usually 200-paged books are WAY too short for me, and salt is a look that should last a long time on me, but I just wanted to end it all?? Right there????<br /><br />I hate travel stories. The travel aspect makes everything so much slower and so much more boring. I also hate epic fantasies, because everything feels too historical-feeling for my taste, and the women are treated horribly. Yeah, I’d rather,,,, not.<br /><br />🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹<br /><br />The characters were interesting enough, I guess. They felt very flat at times and <b>I didn’t feel like they went through much development</b>??? (Except for Froi, and even then it wasn’t that much.)<br /><br />Honestly at this point I’m just questioning who dropped me on my head as a baby for me to be this STUPID to pick this book up?????<br /><br /><b>F*nnikin was boring and also annoying.</b> Male hero who wants to save the day and his country but is also secretly angsty and craves the attention of a female but also refuses the female when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she’s a queen and SHE chooses HIM instead of the other way like the sexist crap he is <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and also is just generally all-around, how you say,,, BORING??? Uhh I think I’ll pass.<br /><br />Evanjalin was the only character I actually LIKED. She was very strong and sassy and she deserved much better than whoever F*nnikin is. Not much development either, but I’ll take <b>strong female characters in fantasy</b>, especially when literally all the other characters are male. Fun.<br /><br />Froi was. uhhhh. Well I liked him, but I would’ve liked him more if Evanjalin hadn’t let him get off easy on him trying to rape her??? And there was literally only ONE time of reprimanding from someone who wasn’t Evanjalin???? No thanks.<br /><br />Then there were some other minor characters, but I don’t care enough about them to talk about them so.<br /><br />🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹<br /><br />On top of literally feeling my life slowly drain away from how much the book dragged, <b>the romance made me want to die even more</b>!!! Strong female characters deserve better than boring, sexist pieces of trash. The cuddling scenes, “gripping her tightly against his chest” scenes, and kissing scenes made me actually choke on my saliva.<br /><br />The plot twists were cool, and I didn’t see them coming. (But then again, I don’t usually see things coming, like how much I’d be disappointed by this book.) But they weren’t SHOCKING??? Like they were definitely a surprise, but <b>unfortunately I really didn’t care</b>, which seems to be a common theme with me.<br /><br />🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹🌷🌹<br /><br />I honestly don’t know why I’m not rating this much lower,, but I think it’s because <b>this book is just very meh</b>. It’s not a great book, but it’s not a HORRIBLE book. I personally wouldn’t recommend it because I almost fell asleep numerous times, and no one should have to put up with F*nnikin for a whole 400 pages. <br /><br />But if you want to try to read this, I literally don’t care. <b>I just don’t want this in my life anymore bye.</b></span>

<div id="review_317536501" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317536501" />
    <a title="Kristalia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia"><img alt="Kristalia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535637983p2/5705623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/317536501?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristalia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristalia " href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia">Kristalia </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kristalia  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=cut-my-heart-out">cut-my-heart-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=be-my-heroes-please">be-my-heroes-please</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorite-couple">favorite-couple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorites-absolute">favorites-absolute</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=wishlist_series">wishlist_series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=sob-fest">sob-fest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer317536501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2400601192690490412"><b> Buddy read with my darlings <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/613289845' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nab</a> & <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/482222393' rel='nofollow noopener'>Basuhi </a> & <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/609901856' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hershey </a> <br/><br/><b>Final rating: 5/5 stars</b><br/><b>Final rating - for the whole series: 5.5/5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote><i><b>“Be prepared for the worst, my love, for it lives next door to the best.”</b></i></blockquote>
<br/><br/><b>This is not the first time that i have read this book. </b>This is my <b>second </b>time and <b><i>i love it as much as i did </i></b>back then. My feelings stayed true to it, and that wont change easily as it seems. So, you should know that i am writing this review while having in mind that i have also read the rest of this</b></span>
  <span id="freeText2400601192690490412" style="display:none"><b> Buddy read with my darlings <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/613289845" rel="nofollow noopener">Nab</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/482222393" rel="nofollow noopener">Basuhi </a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/609901856" rel="nofollow noopener">Hershey </a> <br><br><b>Final rating: 5/5 stars</b><br><b>Final rating - for the whole series: 5.5/5 stars</b><br><br><blockquote><i><b>“Be prepared for the worst, my love, for it lives next door to the best.”</b></i></blockquote>
<br><br><b>This is not the first time that i have read this book. </b>This is my <b>second </b>time and <b><i>i love it as much as i did </i></b>back then. My feelings stayed true to it, and that wont change easily as it seems. So, you should know that i am writing this review while having in mind that i have also read the rest of this series.<br><br><i><b>Melina Marchetta is captivating author. </b></i>I love her stories, her writing style, her characters - basically everything.<i><b> This series is for me one of her best works</b></i>, when looked as one piece. And even though <i><b>this book can be read as standalone</b></i>, i strongly <b><i>encourage you to read the other two </i></b>books in the series too, as they get so much better as the story progresses (after all, they are masterpieces - at least for me). <br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b><i><u>WRITING</u></i></b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br><br>I have to start with writing style -<i><b> it was beautiful, captivating and magical</b></i>. It felt like someone was telling you a story of Lumatere... a country which had fallen under a curse.<br><br><blockquote><i><b> “Because any hope beyond that, my boy, would be too much. I feared we would drown in it.”<br>"Then I choose to drown,” Finnikin said. “In hope. Rather than float into nothing.”<br></b></i></blockquote>
<br><br> I also love how she characterized characters: they all have faces. They are all well developed. <br><br><blockquote><i><b> “Somehow, even in the worst of times, the tiniest fragments of good survive. It was the grip in which one held those fragments that counted.” </b></i></blockquote>
<br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b><i><u>STORY</u></i></b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br><br><i><b>The story is dark and beautiful, there is no other way of saying it.</b></i> I can say that is unique, and also not unique cause i know of only one story similar to this one called <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104089.Tigana" title="Tigana by Guy Gavriel Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">Tigana</a>, but i wouldn't call them the same. <i><b>This story is about a country called Lumatere</b></i>, now cursed land which doesn't allow anyone to enter or to leave. It began with royal family being slayed, and with witch cursing the land in her dying moments. The people in Lumatere are devastated cause they can't get out, and people out of Lumatere suffer because they have no home to go back to. On the other hand, in Lumatere sits an imposter king, terrorizing citizens. And then, there is a prophecy of heir who will return to break the curse. If only there is a heir left in the world. But people of Lumatere won't give up easily - Finnikin of the Rock, Evanjalin of the Novices and Sir Topher travel to find the lost heir to the throne, prince Balthazar.<br><br><i><b>The world building is amazing. Even though when you first read the book, 1/3 of it may seem like info-dump, but i assure you, it all becomes understandable. </b></i><br><br><i><b>I also think that this story is more like a combination between mature young adult and new adult, so you know what to expect. </b></i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b><i><u>CHARACTERS</u></i></b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br>♦ <b><i><u>Finnikin</u></i></b>:<br><br><b><i>Finnikin of the Rock, son of the captain of the King's guard, searches and hopes to find his childhood friend, the rightful heir to the throne, Balthazar. </i></b><br><br>Finn, the main character of the story is not an usual protagonist. I don't love him, but more like him. He had his faults, and for some i blame him, but i also understood him. He wants to believe, but he finds it impossible to do it. He is complicated, maybe sometimes even more complicated that he should have been. But that is what i loved about him.<br><br>♦ <b><i><u>Evanjalin</u></i></b>:<br><br><b><i>Evanjalin of the Novices, who has the ability to walk through the dreams of Lumaterans trapped in their own land, claims to have walked through the dream of the heir, Balthazar.</i></b><br><br>Evanjalin was absolutely complicated, strong leading heroine, and she does everything that she thinks is necessary for things to go as planned, also getting the title "<i>Spawn of the Devil</i>" by Finnikin. I love her, she is just amazing and fantastic character.<br><br><br>♦ <b><i><u>Froi</u></i></b>:<br><br><b><i>Froi is the thief from Sarnak we first encounter in the story. He did some things that cannot be forgotten, but he also reedemed himself as the story went.</i></b><br><br>Froi is one of the characters that is somehow left as a mystery, which is also good, since he is the one the next book is about. And i promise you, his story has so much to deliver. I don't remember how i felt about him before, i can only remember how i feel now, but its clouded since i know his "future" in this series. So, i won't comment him now. <br><br><br>♦ <b><i><u>Trevanion</u></i></b>:<br><br><b><i>Trevanion is the Captain of the King of Lumatere's guard, sent to prison for being who he is, when the impostor king claimed the throne. </i></b><br><br>Trevanion is fascinating, strong father figure and great man. I loved his relationship with Finnikin. <br><br><br>♦ <b><i><u>Sir Topher</u></i></b>:<br><br><b><i>Man respected by others and also like a second father to Finnikin, he travels with Evanjalin and Finn to find the heir. </i></b><br><br>I liked him a lot. That's all.<br><br>♦ <b><i><u>Other characters</u></i></b>:<br><br><b><i>There are so many wonderful characters and all of them were so well done... Lucian, Balthazar, Isaboe, Tessadora, Serannona, each one of them has a story to tell.</i></b><br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b><i><u>OVERALL</u></i></b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br>I cannot help but feel immense love toward this book, especially now that i have reread it - it made so many things clearer. <br><br>If you don't like the first book, keep in mind that they do get better in the second and third book. And although this book could have been read as standalone, second book ends with huge cliffhanger. And the story is filled with so much plot twists and uniqueness that i consider the last two books <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165761.Quintana_of_Charyn__Lumatere_Chronicles___3_" title="Quintana of Charyn (Lumatere Chronicles, #3) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Quintana of Charyn</a> masterpieces.<br>____________________________________________<br><br>● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ●<br>____________________________________________ <br><br><b> MY LUMATERE CHRONICLES REVIEWS: </b><br><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317536501" rel="nofollow noopener"> Finnikin of the Rock (Lumatere Chronicles, #1) </a> <br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317536566" rel="nofollow noopener"> Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) </a> <br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317536614" rel="nofollow noopener"> Quintana of Charyn (Lumatere Chronicles, #3) </a> <br><br><br><br><b><i><br>This review can be found on my blog: <a href="http://infinity-of-time.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">infinity-of-time.blogspot.com</a> also known as... </i></b><br><a href="http://infinity-of-time.blogspot.com/2013/07/finnikin-of-rock-lumatere-chronicles-1.html" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363317i/714576.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4263267802325248865">Set in the beautiful country of Lumatere, Finnikin goes on a quest to find his King and best friend Balthazar. Along on his journey, the beautiful but wild Evanjalin, his mentor and teacher, Sir Topher and thief Froi come together to find the mystery between the country’s impostor king and the biggest secret that is known in the entire kingdom.<br/><br/>Full of adventure, wonderful story telling, highly developed characters and a mystery that will have you wanting more, <em>Finnikan of the Rock</em> is clearly a w</span>
  <span id="freeText4263267802325248865" style="display:none">Set in the beautiful country of Lumatere, Finnikin goes on a quest to find his King and best friend Balthazar. Along on his journey, the beautiful but wild Evanjalin, his mentor and teacher, Sir Topher and thief Froi come together to find the mystery between the country’s impostor king and the biggest secret that is known in the entire kingdom.<br /><br />Full of adventure, wonderful story telling, highly developed characters and a mystery that will have you wanting more, <em>Finnikan of the Rock</em> is clearly a winner. Brilliantly written I highly recommend this fantasy to any <em>Lord of the Rings</em> fan. I love big stories with several plots, and the setting just sounds so unbelievably like the medieval time which I love that I couldn’t help but fall for the characters and their problems.<br /><br />Finnikin is an agreeable character and highly suspicious of Evanjalin for she’s stubborn and always argues with him a lot. In that case, I liked her a lot. Her character is strong-willed and feisty. And you can feel a love story develop a mile away. Froi on the other hand, has so much hurt in his past, which I know after reading the first one, we’re more likely to see him in the next book aptly titled “Froi of the Exiles.”<br /><br />Add this book to your collection book lovers, you won’t be disappointed!</span>

<div id="review_1011615261" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1011615261" />
    <a title="Maxwell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell"><img alt="Maxwell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539318702p2/1381728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1011615261?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxwell" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell">Maxwell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8757361-finnikin-of-the-rock">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1011615261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11218725244095415884">Upon re-reading this, I'm definitely not as enthusiastic about this as I was the first time through. Maybe it's simply because I had read it before, and as I made my way through it a second time I started to remember things and there wasn't that initial reaction to be surprised or delighted by. But I've also read a lot of books multiple times where that feeling holds up, and for some reason it just didn't really do that for me with this book. Nevertheless, I still think this is underrated and ex</span>
  <span id="freeText11218725244095415884" style="display:none">Upon re-reading this, I'm definitely not as enthusiastic about this as I was the first time through. Maybe it's simply because I had read it before, and as I made my way through it a second time I started to remember things and there wasn't that initial reaction to be surprised or delighted by. But I've also read a lot of books multiple times where that feeling holds up, and for some reason it just didn't really do that for me with this book. Nevertheless, I still think this is underrated and excellent YA fantasy novel. And I am looking forward to finally finishing the series. I love the characters so much; they're really what kept me going through this. If initially I gave this a 4.5-5 stars, I'd probably knock it down to a solid 4 after re-reading it.<br />----------------------<br />Amazing. Go read this now. <br />Full review to come. <br />----------------------<br /><br />Alright folks, let's just cut to the chase: this is the <i>most underrated book I've ever read.</i> Yup, I said it. Sure there are over 17,000 ratings of it here on Goodreads, but for people I know personally, only <b>one</b> person has ever talked about it enough to make me pick it up. (So thank you Regan, thank you).<br /><br />This is YA Fantasy. But this isn't just any old YA Fantasy. This is YA Fantasy at it's <u>finest</u>.<br /><br /><i>Finnikin of the Rock</i> is a story that captivated me from the prologue. Yeah, the short few pages at the beginning of the book that tells a cryptic, confusing, but creative tale of three boys making a blood oath, seriously captivated me. I just knew that I had to keep reading to find out what these boys were promising, and what would happen, and how it would all end up!<br /><br />The main part of the book picks up ten years after the prologue. Finnikin is traveling with Sir Topher, after the unspeakable happens in Lumatere: the impostor king from Charyn, a neighboring land, has invaded the country, killed all the royal family, and taken the land for himself. It's terrible, and gripping. <br /><br />Finnikin, now in the present day feels a calling to travel to the Cloister of Lagrami in Sendecane. There he meets Evanjalin, a young novice who joins him and Sir Topher on their trip.<br /><br />This is a lot of explanation, so that's all I'm going to leave you with. <b>Just read the book!</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>My Thoughts:</u>
</b><br /><br />1. World-building: incredible. The history of the land, the images Marchetta writes, everything is so vivid. And it all makes sense. Everything has a justification and explanation. Nothing just happens <i>because</i>, it happens with realistic reasoning. It's very rich in detail.<br /><br />2. Characters: Finnikin is snarky, strong, smart, but also a bit hot-headed at times. He is likeable, like the shy, quiet guy in your class who occasionally takes a stand for what he things is right (if that makes sense). Evanjalin is one tough chick. I like her, a lot. All the secondary characters are well built, and as the story progresses you get more and more backstory and a feel for them as people, rather than just supporting characters.<br /><br />3. Plot: it's always exciting. Even if nothing is really happening, the story is engaging and the <b>dialogue</b> is excellent. It tells enough of the story without being obvious or unnecessary, and it always fits the characterization well. Love it.<br /><br />Overall you can probably tell I'm now obsessed with this book (in fact, I'm already 1/3 of the way through the second book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a> as I am writing this!). <br /><br />4.5/5- would <i>obviously</i> recommend. Duh. Go read it, please!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11218725244095415884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_485258565" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485258565" />
    <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday"><img alt="Ash Wednesday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379043440p2/10484016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/485258565?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash Wednesday" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8757361-finnikin-of-the-rock">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=awesome-heroines">awesome-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=sounds-like-a-tv">sounds-like-a-tv</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer485258565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12749275773393909902"><i>
  <b>4 STARS<br/><blockquote>”You asked me once what my magic was.<br/>That is my magic.”</blockquote></b>
</i><br/>I am now convinced Melina Marchetta is made of equal parts freshly-baked cookies, clean laundry, pixie dust and waffles. Something about her books just comforts me in ways I cannot attempt to capture into words. Her oeuvre covers themes that in their simplicity would probably come across emotionally exploitative in lesser hands, but her crafty storytelling effortlessly ties textured characters with my personal reflexes and sentime</span>
  <span id="freeText12749275773393909902" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>4 STARS<br><blockquote>”You asked me once what my magic was.<br>That is my magic.”</blockquote></b>
</i><br>I am now convinced Melina Marchetta is made of equal parts freshly-baked cookies, clean laundry, pixie dust and waffles. Something about her books just comforts me in ways I cannot attempt to capture into words. Her oeuvre covers themes that in their simplicity would probably come across emotionally exploitative in lesser hands, but her crafty storytelling effortlessly ties textured characters with my personal reflexes and sentiments towards family, courage, hope and love. <br><br>And somewhere in the middle a bit of magic happens.<br><br>As with fantasy books, it all started with a blood (and hair - courtesy of Isaboe, Balthazar’s younger sister) promise. Prince Balthazar of Lumatere pledged to die defending his royal house, his cousin Lucian of the Monts swore to be their beacon in times of need and his friend Finnikin of the Rock vowed to be their protector and guide for as long as he lived. <i>Finnkin of the Rock</i> chronicles Finnkin’s conflict in fulfilling that vow amidst despair and hopelessness ten years after Lumatere was besieged by the Impostor King sending half their peoples scattered all throughout Skuldenore while their last remaining royal, Balthazar, is nowhere to be seen. They travel to the Cloister of Lagrami where a novice named Evanjalin claims to walk in the dreams of the remaining Lumaterans within the walls has walked into Prince Balthazar’s dream.<br><br>While I’ve read (and loved) nearly all her contemporary books, it took me a bit of time to brave The Lumatere Chronicles. And by the way, <b>I’M HOLDING EACH AND EVERY FRIEND OF MINE HERE WHO DIDN’T TIE ME DOWN AND FORCED ME TO READ THIS SOONER, RESPONSIBLE FOR THIS TRAVESTY.</b> Mostly because being familiar with her narrative, fitting that particular style in High Fantasy feels a little… overwhelming. I mean, can you imagine this being told the way <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road" title="On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Jellicoe Road</a> is written? Someone is bound to lose hair over that: pulled or shed. Thankfully this story unfurled in a more or less straightforward almost heist-like manner. Where Finnikin, Evanjalin and Sir Topher gathers the necessary implements and pieces to their fractured hopes to get their people home.<br><br>Though certainly, Marchetta's fingerprint is still all over the place: Trevonian and Beatriss had a little of Sam and Georgie while the way the five days of the unspeakable was revealed is pretty much the standard in her books. She writes these characters with such a lovely insight in each and how they relate to each other: fathers and sons, friends and enemies, teachers and apprentices, orphans and the world. And lest you think this is just too heavy…<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>”Hungry,” Froi muttered.<br>“And we’re not?” Finnikin snapped back.<br>“He’s a boy,” Sir Topher admonished, “who needs to eat. You were the same at his age Finnikin.”<br>“No I was not.”<br>Sir Topher snorted with disbelief.<br>“All of you stay here,” Finnikin ordered. “I will get us food.” He pointed a finger at his father. “No fighting with the locals!”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>Her perspective is very matriarchal and feminist (that scene where Yata asked Finnikin to meet Lady Abie, Beatriss and Tesadora makes me think of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7417780.The_Piper_s_Son" title="The Piper's Son by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">The Piper's Son</a>), but the male characters don’t feel compromised. A very narrow buffer range that doesn’t exist where Marchetta’s concerned.<br><br>How does she do it? Why are there so many EL James clones and none of hers????<br><br>The scope of the encompassing story of Lumatere was vast, with some Old Testament-y feel to it (I could almost imagine someone crying <i>“Let my People go!”</i> in one scene). The way Finnikin and his crew travelled from one region to another getting themselves enmeshed in the politics and nuanced conflicts in that particular area gave this the gritty adventure I’d most expect in adult HF. Much like in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839976.Red_Rising__Red_Rising_Trilogy___1_" title="Red Rising (Red Rising Trilogy, #1) by Pierce Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Rising</a>, I’ve had to check several times that this is young adult because it certainly didn’t have that feel you get from the usual suspects in this genre: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3236307.Graceling__Graceling_Realm___1_" title="Graceling (Graceling Realm, #1) by Kristin Cashore" rel="nofollow noopener">Graceling</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429092.The_Girl_of_Fire_and_Thorns__Fire_and_Thorns___1_" title="The Girl of Fire and Thorns (Fire and Thorns, #1) by Rae Carson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl of Fire and Thorns</a>… this is perched way above whatever benchmark those fairytales set for themselves. This wears the grown-up pants quite comfortably. I loved it but that may very well be this book’s gift and it’s curse.<br><br>Because of the maturity in the story, the characters and the themes this chose to focus on, certain plot points felt off-key and an ill-fit to what this set out to do. I think most of the review here didn’t appreciate that reveal around the 75% mark and what came after. I actually loved that plot twist. I WANTED that plot twist <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[These were my first two highlights in the book:<br><blockquote><i>The three friends spent all summer digging the trap, and when it was finished, they dragged Balthazar’s youngest sister, Princess Isaboe, along to be bait.</i></blockquote>
<br>-and-<br><blockquote><i>… and they cut flesh from their bodies and tugged a strand of hair from the weeping Isaboe’s head to make a sacrifice for their goddess/</i></blockquote>
<br>I liked Evanjalin fine but I was a fan of Isaboe’s story first.<br><br>Okay I liked Evanjalin most of the time. Especially when she’s not acting like a jealous non-girlfriend over Finnikin’s whoring after he survived the prison she sent him to in order to motivate Trevanion to escape. A prison where he could have been raped and beaten down. Repeatedly. I mean jebus cut the guy some slack, woman! But despite her messianic complex going on, that dose of manipulation and willingness to go far and beyond for her people, the intentions of her character doesn’t feel contrived or offensively perfect to me. Yes Madrigal, I’m looking at you.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>So when that reveal came, I was a little disappointed with how the explanation felt a little anaemic. Almost as much as the elaborate explanation behind Evanjalin’s abilities. <br><br>The POVs jump around a lot but didn’t deter me from forging emotional bonds with most of the characters. What was a little distracting was that there were visible holes in certain scenes where say Sir Topher orders Finnikin to go this way and the POV follows Finnikin on that adventure, but I’m left wondering, what’s Sir Topher doing while all that is happening? It created some lapses in the continuity, as if all the world stops with that character’s POV. <br><br>The plight of the Lumaterans greatly outweighed my interest over the romance, if you can believe it. Though make no mistake, the romance was good and there were more than one occasion when I felt some swelling in my heart over characters being reunited and truths being revealed. The side-plots were mesmerising (Team Perri/Tesadora! Woohoo!) but it was that pervading theme of the despair and sorrow by the exiles, their heart-wrenching past and their losses in the present more than filled the very few points where this lacked.<br><br>Gah, I’ve blathered on far too long yet again! So hard to review High Fantasy concisely! Okay needless to say I loved it. I foresee a re-read down the line but I’m more looking forward to reading about Froi. <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>Froi liked the way Moss said “our boy” as if Froi belonged to them instead of belonging to no one. Sometimes during their travels, he had imagined there was someone inside Lumatere searching for him. But there had been no mother like Lady Abian or father like Trevanion waiting. No kin who recognised him as theirs.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397903980ra/9344310.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Last thing:<br>Goddess of Light = <b>LAGRAMI</b><br>Goddess of Dark = <b>SAGRAMI</b><br>Goddess Complete = <b>SALAMI</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397904321ra/9344361.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="http://ashwednesday.booklikes.com/post/858329/the-church-of-melina-marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Also on BookLikes.</a><br><br>--------------------------------<br><br>Dat charmer of an ending.<br><br><b>FUCK THA (squee) PO-LICE!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395735181ra/9037319.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Review to follow after the negotiations.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12749275773393909902" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1219181360" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1219181360" />
    <a title="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source"><img alt="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586156113p2/6511257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1219181360?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" href="/user/show/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source">Sue (Hollywood News Source)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780763652920" href="/book/show/10636358-finnikin-of-the-rock">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=interracial-romance">interracial-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=characters-of-color">characters-of-color</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=favorite-otps">favorite-otps</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=friendship-goals">friendship-goals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=alert-the-authorities-i-ship-it">alert-the-authorities-i-ship-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=family">family</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1219181360" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16014654868052886325"><strong>I proclaim this is the year, I fell in love with Melina Marchetta.</strong><br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448945694ra/17211799.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><em>A fair warning to everyone, this is not a full review of any of the books, but instead a quick overview discussing what, I find thought provoking about the series. </em><br/><br/><em>This is a spoiler free analysis.<br/><br/>Proceed with caution.</em><br/><br/><strong>Lumatere Chronicles are a radical, progressive tale about a nation trying to restore their honor.</strong><br/><br/><em>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1219181360' rel='nofollow noopener'>Finnikin of the Rock</a>
</em> is a great introduction to hesitant readers who’s slowly grasping the concept of the series. I</span>
  <span id="freeText16014654868052886325" style="display:none"><strong>I proclaim this is the year, I fell in love with Melina Marchetta.</strong><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448945694ra/17211799.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><em>A fair warning to everyone, this is not a full review of any of the books, but instead a quick overview discussing what, I find thought provoking about the series. </em><br><br><em>This is a spoiler free analysis.<br><br>Proceed with caution.</em><br><br><strong>Lumatere Chronicles are a radical, progressive tale about a nation trying to restore their honor.</strong><br><br><em>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1219181360" rel="nofollow noopener">Finnikin of the Rock</a>
</em> is a great introduction to hesitant readers who’s slowly grasping the concept of the series. It was beautifully written, filled with remarkable characters and gripping plot. <strong>Readers would get <strong>more than what they asked for. </strong></strong>I am simply blown away by its simplicity and spot on narration.<br><br>The sequel, <em><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1221637437" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a> </em>is quite difficult to rate. I thoroughly liked it. As a matter of fact, this is where, I met one of my favorite female characters, Phaedra. But, I still find some of the parts lacking. I supposed because I was expecting to form a firm attachment to the new characters. Though, don’t fret because the next installment would be a better company.<br><br>The concluding book,<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1233397974" rel="nofollow noopener"> <em>Quintana of Charyn</em></a>, on the other hand is the deal breaker. Marchetta skillfully wrapped up Lumatere Chronicles.<br><br><strong>Marchetta deftly established the cultural background, significance, and differences of each nation.</strong><strong> It truly shows within the subtle, but rich world building in the text. </strong><br><br>Per instance, Phaedra’s accent compared to the native Lumaterean intonation, the rich and diverse languages and vocabulary differs when it comes to various countries. How their clothing and land looks like. What are their traditions and vital livelihood, the color of their skin and more.<br><br><strong>Marchetta’s political message was deliberate and calculated.</strong><br><br><strong>Lumatere Chronicles also tackled the animosity between societies. Racism, sexism and classism.</strong><br><br>Here's one of my favorite passages from Froi of the Exiles. What a very powerful scene. I couldn't highlight it enough.<br><blockquote>“<em>They meant no harm</em>,” <em>she heard</em> Tesadora say at <em>her shoulder</em>.<br><br>Phaedra walked away, scrubbing away tears, not realising she was crying. She was tired of feeling shame. She was tired of feeling helpless all the time.<br><br>"Did you hear what I said?" Tesadora asked, gripping her arm.<br><br>" They say were dirty," Phaedra cried, pulling free. "Luci-en says were useless. Your queen says were murderers. I overheard the Mont lads say we should be rounded up and set aflame. Were barren. We worship too many gods. Our bread is tasteless. Our faces are plain. We cry too much. Our fathers abandon us. We dont understand kinship. Were pitiful!"<br><br>Phaedra shook her head. "If your people mean no offence, they should not speak their thoughts out loud in front of their children, Tesadora. Because it will be their children who come to slaughter us one day, all because of the careless words passed down by their elders who meant no harm."<br><br>Tesadora stared a moment and then a ghost of a smile appeared on her face.<br><br>"Strange things happen when we stand face to face with our enemy, dont they, Phaedra of Alonso?"</blockquote><br>The unsurprising thing that strikes me about this saga,<strong> Marchetta didn’t shy away from her usual brand. </strong><strong>Who would have ever thought a high fantasy series would also touch the ache, loneliness, and depression with a strong emphasis?</strong> It usually gets swept under the rug for the sake of the swashbuckling, tyranny story line. But, Lumatere Chronicles have so many interweaving threads, a reader can’t seem to take a break.<br><br>In addition, to this series’ handful of depth and layers, this story is highly fueled by its remarkable characters. I love how Marchetta illustrates the deep and fragility of family and friendship.<br><br><strong>From its brilliant world building, bloody politics, the portrayal of justice and feminism. I would heartily recommend Lumatere Chronicles to readers who are looking for a classic high fantasy book. </strong><br><br>Review also posted at <a>Hollywood News Source.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16014654868052886325" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
