<div id="review_124680224" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124680224" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124680224?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Graceling and Fire</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Arlene by: </span>
      Gift from Alexa - Thank you!!
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=aussie">aussie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124680224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12672150936887316953"><i> “Finn, listen!” Trevanion (Finnikin’s father) said, his voice raw. “I prayed to see you one more time. It’s all I prayed for. Nothing more. And my prayers were answered. Go east, I’ll lead them west.”<br/><br/>“We have a dilemma, then,” Finnikin said fiercely. “Because I prayed that you would grow old and hold my children in your arms as you held me. My prayers have not been answered yet, Trevanion. So whose prayer is more worthy? Yours or mine?” </i><br/><br/><br/>Melina Marchetta fan club??? Sign me up now! If she has mo</span>
  <span id="freeText12672150936887316953" style="display:none"><i> “Finn, listen!” Trevanion (Finnikin’s father) said, his voice raw. “I prayed to see you one more time. It’s all I prayed for. Nothing more. And my prayers were answered. Go east, I’ll lead them west.”<br /><br />“We have a dilemma, then,” Finnikin said fiercely. “Because I prayed that you would grow old and hold my children in your arms as you held me. My prayers have not been answered yet, Trevanion. So whose prayer is more worthy? Yours or mine?” </i><br /><br /><br />Melina Marchetta fan club??? Sign me up now! If she has more <b>Finnikin of the Rock</b> type books up her sleeve, my pocketbook is in a world of hurt because OMG this book blew my mind away and tugged at my heart the entire time! I haven’t taken this type of fantastical journey since Cashore’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3236307.Graceling__The_Seven_Kingdoms___1_" title="Graceling (The Seven Kingdoms, #1) by Kristin Cashore" rel="nofollow noopener">Graceling</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6001758.Fire__The_Seven_Kingdoms___2_" title="Fire (The Seven Kingdoms, #2) by Kristin Cashore" rel="nofollow noopener">Fire</a>. <br /><br />Marchetta’s writing is magical, flawless and top tier in her genre. She has a seamless ability to catapult her readers into an undefined time that feels both medieval and mythical with a hint of realism that keeps you grounded to the here and now.. Her characters are witty with just the right amount of snark, which is my preferred method of communication. I loved Finnikin and Evanjelin. Their journey through <i>The Land of Skuldendore</i> was filled with intrigue and most of all hope for the people of Lumatere.<br /><br />About the book: At the age of nine, Finnikin received a prophecy from the gods that warned him about the destruction of his homeland Lumatere. So Finnikin, Prince Balthazar, and the prince’s cousin Lucian, bonded together at the rock to make a blood sacrifice to keep their home safe. Despite their plea to the gods, the ‘five days of the unspeakable’ occurred and Lumatere was destroyed and the royal family was slaughtered. After ten years in exile, Finnikin is led once again to a rock to meet a novice, Evanjalin, who is plagued by dreams of those held behind the walls of Lumatere waiting for someone to rescue them and return their land of light. <br /><br />This book makes me feel quite conflicted because as I rage on and blast authors that can’t seem to write a stand-alone book now-a-days. However, <b>Finnikin of the Rock</b> is one that I feel is worthy of sequels because simply put, I ♥ Finn. What a great book that deserves to be read NOW and continue on for quite some time. I’ll be sure to keep my eye out for more of Marchetta’s fictional magic.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12672150936887316953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_153509905" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/153509905" />
    <a title="Limonessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa"><img alt="Limonessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424025988p2/4147373.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/153509905?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Limonessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Limonessa" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa">Limonessa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=australian">australian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153509905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3892322685403485745"><i>
  <b>"Everything is evil that humans can't control or conquer"</b>
</i><br/><br/>What kind of book is Finnikin of the Rock?<br/><br/>It's a fantasy book. Evidently.<br/>It's a love story. Certainly. <br/>But not only. <br/><br/>It all starts with three friends, a prophetic dream and a blood pledge. <br/>It continues with an invasion, a terrible curse and the struggle of one people to take back what they lost.<br/><br/>For me Finnikin of the Rock is a book about <b>identities</b>. About a people, the Lumaterans, losing their national identity and fighting to get it b</span>
  <span id="freeText3892322685403485745" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"Everything is evil that humans can't control or conquer"</b>
</i><br /><br />What kind of book is Finnikin of the Rock?<br /><br />It's a fantasy book. Evidently.<br />It's a love story. Certainly. <br />But not only. <br /><br />It all starts with three friends, a prophetic dream and a blood pledge. <br />It continues with an invasion, a terrible curse and the struggle of one people to take back what they lost.<br /><br />For me Finnikin of the Rock is a book about <b>identities</b>. About a people, the Lumaterans, losing their national identity and fighting to get it back, about a man who's been imprisoned for 10 years and has lost his identity, about a girl who is concealing hers to save her country and about a boy who really doesn't know who he is. <br /><br />In unmistakeable Marchetta's style, we are presented with a book that not only has got an intriguing plot, is full of action scenes, adventure, amazing and detailed worldbuilding, and as usual, characterization like only Marchetta can do, but also with a book with an underlying message that goes beyond our mere entertainment as readers.<br />It is a condemnation of war and of its horrors, it denounces persecutions for political, ethnic or religious reasons, it opens a window on people, at any latitude and climate, whose dignity has been taken away together with their homeland.<br />The words <i>mass graves</i> and <i>ethnical cleansing</i> are words which will be stuck in your throat during some passages of this book and I dare you not feel compassionate for the Lumateran people. <br /><br />So, end in end, this is a book that is only <i>disguised</i> as fantasy but that, in reality, is well above that. <br />It's probably superfluous to say that I really loved this book and I can't wait to read its sequel coming out in October. <br /><br />My favorite passage:<br /><br /><i>"Because without our language, we have lost ourselves. Who are we without our words?"</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3892322685403485745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14625474273058760660">3.5 Stars... I think? <br/><br/>I'm having a hard time pinning down what I didn't like about this story. There really is so much to rave about... so many beautiful moments. <b>The character depth is MIND BLOWING phenomenal.</b> The world building is just so many layers of fascinating. The plot twists are tear jerkingly gorgeous. <br/><br/><b>So why only 3 stars?</b> Bah. Okay. I've been thinking about this for a while.. and here's the best explanation I can offer: <b>I felt like a 3rd party viewer- sitting in the stands, watching e</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14625474273058760660" style="display:none">3.5 Stars... I think? <br /><br />I'm having a hard time pinning down what I didn't like about this story. There really is so much to rave about... so many beautiful moments. <b>The character depth is MIND BLOWING phenomenal.</b> The world building is just so many layers of fascinating. The plot twists are tear jerkingly gorgeous. <br /><br /><b>So why only 3 stars?</b> Bah. Okay. I've been thinking about this for a while.. and here's the best explanation I can offer: <b>I felt like a 3rd party viewer- sitting in the stands, watching events happen. I never felt like I was <i>in</i> them. Like I was watching them from afar. </b> <br /><br />Additionally, the pace was quite slow; and the story is told from multiple POVs -and I just felt like when I was finally connecting to Finnikin or Evanjalin.. the POV would swap and I would have to read another several pages before I get back in with them. <br /><br />Please, please do not let this keep you from reading the story. It is very emotional and very driven. It is worth a go. (Even if it is for the astounding amount of beautiful quotes.)<br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/herbookishthings/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17237727534345921990"><b>Be prepared for the worst my love, for it lives next door to the best</b><br/><br/><i>Words fail me, Yes..I..can't...find...the...right...words, to express how shockingly raw, deep and unequivocally flawless my first read from Melina Marchetta was. I'm still like this after this read:</i><br/><a href='http://s284.photobucket.com/user/kellsway/media/3fangirling_zpsw82eokk2.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

  <span id="freeText17237727534345921990" style="display:none"><b>Be prepared for the worst my love, for it lives next door to the best</b><br><br><i>Words fail me, Yes..I..can't...find...the...right...words, to express how shockingly raw, deep and unequivocally flawless my first read from Melina Marchetta was. I'm still like this after this read:</i><br><a href="http://s284.photobucket.com/user/kellsway/media/3fangirling_zpsw82eokk2.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456186177ra/18201150.gif" alt=" photo 3fangirling_zpsw82eokk2.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Guys I cried, laughed, curse, fought and fell in love alongside these wonderful characters. Please take my advice and stick with this book, even though I found it to start off just a tad dull. I shutter to think the gigantic mistake that I would have made if I had DNF this thing of beauty to early.</i><br><br><i>Finnikin, Evanjalin, Sir Topher, Froi, Trevanion and Perri are just are few of the characters in this book that I fell in love with. I must confessed that I did dislike our lead heroine Evanjalin at first but as her character developed I started to appreciate her role and place in the storyline. Finnikin was a very strong male lead and I took to him from the get go. I couldn't get enough of the world building and I found the story line to be sufficiently solid to leave me wanting more.</i><br><br><i>I give all the stars in the world to Froi,(even though he was not the main lead ) for stealing my heart. I loved how his character grew throughout this book. It was nice experiencing all his grittiness and be part of his slow transformation. His rawness in expressing his feelings was refreshing and was a constant source of comic relief for me. Can't wait to move unto book two to find out more about his story.</i><br><br><b>My Ratings:</b><br><a href="http://s284.photobucket.com/user/kellsway/media/5-Star_zpsd5h1yaoh.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('s+QkSUy8eh1cqmklK03Zh8klOafE7Dxyo6pxD2FV5xudbdude5l7MTL3fk4YLmzT0lwdtK2SlHgrf48M84a9iw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6YUyp2K0hZuGXrbQ/nVZmf+YGEV8YHENQGPoGg81TPzHDM1zVZGEt+gDobvNFuzN5OE8VhUe2QfIthYZneYWbA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta">About Melina Marchetta</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1277655889p3/47104.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9012989710628251425">Melina Marchetta was born in Sydney Australia. Her first novel, Looking For Alibrandi was awarded the Children's Book Council of Australia award in 1993 and her second novel, Saving Francesca won the same award in 2004. Looking For Alibrandi was made into a major film in 2000 and won the Australian Film Institute Award for best Film and best adapted screen play, also written by the author. On the </span>
  <span id="freeText9012989710628251425" style="display:none">Melina Marchetta was born in Sydney Australia. Her first novel, Looking For Alibrandi was awarded the Children's Book Council of Australia award in 1993 and her second novel, Saving Francesca won the same award in 2004. Looking For Alibrandi was made into a major film in 2000 and won the Australian Film Institute Award for best Film and best adapted screen play, also written by the author. On the Jellicoe Road was released in 2006 and won the US Printz Medal in 2009 for excellence in YA literature. This was followed up by Finnikin of the Rock in 2008 which won the Aurealis Award for YA fantasy, The Piper's Son in 2010 which was shortlisted for the Qld Premier's Lit Award, NSW Premier's Lit Award, Prime Minister's Literary Awards, CBC awards and longlisted for the Miles Franklin Award. Her follow up to Finnikin, Froi of the Exiles and Quintana of Charyn were released in 2012 and 2013. Her latest novel Tell the Truth, Shame the Devil is an adult crime novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9012989710628251425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
